Do you have non-Danish-speaking workers on the construction sites? 
- if yes, do you ever experience problems with communication with them? 
Arkil does have non-Danish-speaking workers on the construction sites. The way they tackle 
this is by translating the different signs and posts, but Arkil still believes that there is an 
issue in communication due to the fact that many of the workers are actually dyslexic [51]. 
Enemærke & Pedersen mainly employ Danish speaking workers. But in the cases where it is 
necessary to employ non-Danish-speaking workers, they have a requirement set up where 
the workers must have a representative that can speak Danish. So far that method has 
turned out well for them [54]. 
NCC does have non-Danish-speaking workers on the construction sites, there isn’t enough 
Danish speaking workers available. They also have a requirement set up where the workers 
must have a representative that can speak English [55]. 
Tscherning also have non-Danish-speaking workers on the construction sites that they rent 
from another company. The way they tackle this, is by translating the different signs and 
posts and when other issues arise, they have a contact person from the rental company that 
they can contact [57]. 
 
Do you guys have any consequences set up from your side for when workers fail to comply 
with the safety rules on the construction sites? 
The consequences Arkil has set up for workers who repeatedly fail to comply with the safety 
rules on the construction sites, is via a verbal warning, then a written warning, and then 
finally a firing/expulsion [51]. 
The consequences Enemærke & Pedersen have set up is similar. A verbal warning, followed 
by a written warning, followed by a firing/expulsion [54]. 
NCC also have similar system with a verbal warning, followed by a written warning, followed 
by a firing/expulsion [55]. 
Tscherning also have similar system if workers do not wear the required safety gear or 
follow safety guidelines [57]. 
 
Unions 
Do you think that’s accidents on construction sites happen often, and is still a major 
problem? 
3F states that accidents in the construction industry are twice as frequent compared to the 
rest of the labor market, and the accidents are far more severe than the average. They also 
tend to result in their employees being out sick and losing money in terms of lost 
production. 3F states that this is a problem they have not managed to change in the last 30 
years [67]. 
==PAGE:44==
Page 43 of 246 
 
Bygherreforeningen believes that accidents are still a major problem, and the number of 
death accidents are unfortunately still rising, despite the different approaches they have 
taken to tackle the safety on construction sites [60]. 
Dansk Industri, also believe that accidents are far too common in the construction industry 
and occur more frequently compared to other industries. Dansk Industri thinks that the 
nature of the industry plays a huge role in creating situations that could lead to potential 
hazards [68]. 
 
What types of accidents do you experience, or have you heard of, happens most on 
construction sites? 
3F states that the most common accidents in the construction industry are related to falls, 
both falls on the same level and from one level to another. The falls are largely due to the 
fact that there is a lot of movement taking place in a constantly changing workplace. 
Unfortunately, this means that there often are a lot of objects on a construction site, and 
there are many changes in elevation during the construction process. Workers typically take 
many steps in a workday, which increases the risk e.g., craftsmen often carry objects, which 
also reduces visibility of the walking areas and could increase the chances of accidents. [67] 
The most common accidents that Bygherreforeningen hears about are falling from heights 
and cutting accidents [60]. 
Dansk Industri also states that the most common accident types are falling from heights and 
cutting accidents. Another common accident type is unintentional movement and physical 
wear due to repetitive tasks [68]. 
 
Do you think that accidents where vehicles or cranes are involved, is something that happens 
often, and is a major problem? 
3F states that since there is a large number of vehicles and machinery there is an inherent 
risk of accidents involving vehicles and machinery. Fortunately, most of the machine 
operators are skilled and experienced, there are also requirements for certifications to 
operate larger machinery. But unfortunately, accidents involving vehicles and machinery still 
occur [67]. 
The only vehicle related accidents that Bygherreforeningen hears about, are trucks that 
have tilted over. And this often happens when the trucks arrive on the construction site 
outside of working hours, and there is no worker on site to guide them, which leads them to 
offload on uneven ground, which results in overturning. This also a problem since there is no 
one on site to help the truckdriver if they get injured. From what the interviewee has 
gathered from the statistics from The Danish Working Environment Authority, there has also 
been some collision accidents related to vehicles, but not something that the interviewee 
knows about in detail [60]. 
==PAGE:45==
Page 44 of 246 
 
Dansk Industri states that accidents involving vehicles and machinery are not very common 
in Denmark, but when it does happen, it is something that has fatal consequences [68]. 
 
Do you guys do anything from your side to prevent accidents and improve the safety on 
construction sites? 
- If yes, what do you do? 
3F provides multiple training courses for their members and provides guidance in various 
local departments across the country. They are currently running a 3-year project where five 
employees are dedicated solely to visiting construction sites and assisting members of the 
union with their safety. This is their direct preventive effort. Furthermore, 3F actively 
participates in several organizations with the task to prevent and mitigate accidents. 3F is 
collaborating with Byggeriets Arbejdsmiljøbus (BAMBUS), which is a secretariat with 10 field 
consultants. These consultants can be called upon by both their employers and members to 
provide solution-oriented advice. 3F also works with the joint Industrial Health and Safety 
Group for Construction and Civil Engineering (BFA-BA), which is also impartial and 
collaborates with the parties involved and the Danish Working Environment Authority. They 
develop and distribute comprehensive industry-specific guidance materials that are 
approved by all stakeholders in the construction industry as "best practice." The Danish 
Working Environment Authority often refers to BFA materials, and inspections are 
frequently based on individual industry guidelines. 3F are working on a project called Under 
the safety helmets (Under Hjelmene), which is a joint occupational health and safety 
newspaper published twice a year, that aims to address specific issues in the construction 
industry and focus on the latest developments in rules, legislation, etc. The newspaper has 
approximately 40,000 copies and is well known throughout the industry [67]. 
Bygherreforeningen have just launched a collaboration which focuses on the World Goals. It 
is not specifically related to accidents, but to work environments in general. Furthermore, 
they host courses and seminars that relate to work environment and safety. They are also 
observers on an industry community for work environment, where they contribute as much 
as possible (BFA-BA). They are also a part of BAMBUS, where they also contribute [60]. 
Dansk Industri works with the joint Industrial Health and Safety Group for Construction and 
Civil Engineering (BFA-BA). They are also a part of BAMBUS [68]. 
 
Do you think you could have more measures in place to improve the safety on construction 
sites? 
- If yes, what do you have in mind? 
3F states that they do everything that they can to improve safety on a general level by 
advocating for stricter occupational health and safety legislation, raising political awareness, 
and engaging in discussions with local companies. But as a labor union they have very little 
direct influence on the individual safety of their members. It is a task that individuals must 
take responsibility for themselves, with the assistance of their workplace safety 
representatives and their employers, who ultimately bear the responsibility. 3F states that 
==PAGE:46==
Page 45 of 246 
 
the working environment is complex, because there are many regulations that are not 
entirely black and white and interpretation and compliance with these regulations vary 
significantly [67]. 
Bygherreforeningen believes that they can do more than they already do, but they have to 
prioritize their efforts since they have a lot of areas where they want to do more. Some of 
the things they do occasionally is to try and get more funding, which then can result in them 
having the capacity to add more efforts in relation to work environment and safety [60]. 
Dansk Industri thinks there is always room for more effort to improve the safety on a 
general level. Like changing the working culture of individual professional groups working 
separately within their own field to see beyond their own task and look at the project as 
whole [68]. 
 
What are your opinions on the implementation of advanced technology, such as location-
based GPS sensors and cameras worn by workers and installed in vehicles, as a tool to 
improve the safety on construction sites and to prevent of accidents? 
3F has a positive opinion about the concept. They believe in the potential of sensors in the 
field of occupational health and safety and see them as a powerful tool. 3F are certain that 
it is an area that will be expanded significantly in the coming years to improve the safety on 
construction sites [67]. 
Bygherreforeningen believe that all technology that can help digitalize and automate 
different processes on the construction sites would have a big potential and could help the 
workers by assisting them and result in many things will no longer be dependent on an 
individual person, and therefor be less prone to errors. The same goes for cameras and 
sensor on vehicles, they believe that the concept would help reduce accidents on 
construction sites [60]. 
Dansk Industri can see the big potential that implementation of advanced technologies can 
provide. It would specifically help with monitoring and analyzing movement behavior of 
workers for better safety planning and understanding close encounter incidents [68]. 
 
What do you think your members’/customers’ opinions on this would be? 
3F states that there is a downside of the use of GPS and sensors, specifically cameras in the 
construction industry. This type of monitoring can be perceived as surveillance for the 
workers and can have consequences for their wage conditions and even lead to 
terminations. 3F is also concerned about the data being strictly regulated by the General 
Data Protection Regulation (GDPR), which imposes extensive requirements on how 
employers handle collected data. 3F is already dealing with these types of issues, recently 
they concluded a survey where members were asked about surveillance. 71% of 
respondents from the Construction Group stated that they are subject to surveillance while 
driving company vehicles [67]. 
 
==PAGE:47==
Page 46 of 246 
 
Bygherreforeningen mentions that the majority of project owners would like to know what 
goes on, on their construction sites. The interviewee does not believe that any of their 
members would have a negative opinion on the concept, as they realize the positive 
potential it can bring [60]. 
Dansk Industri are also concerned about the workers perception of being monitored and 
how to handle GDPR [68]. 
 
Do you think that the implementation of this technology realistically could improve the 
safety on construction sites? 
3F are certain that the implementation of sensor technology could reduce the chances of 
vehicle related accidents. To have machines that automatically stop if they detect that they 
are about to hit a colleague, run over a cable, or knock something over. Here technology can 
be a tremendous help in preventing potentially tragic accidents. As long as it is done right 
ethically [67]. 
Bygherreforeningen believe that the concept realistically could improve the safety on 
construction sites but acknowledges that this kind of technology still have ways to go, and 
will continue so for a long time [60]. 
Dansk Industri are positive that the concept will be a beneficial tool in both resource 
management and safety planning [68]. 
 
Do you think that the implementation of this technology will be worth it in spite of the 
expenses that could occur with the installation and maintenance of these technologies? 
3F states that their members don't have any expenses related to this implementation but in 
general the construction industry doesn’t have a high margin profit and therefor investment 
in technologies that don’t have a direct effect on a positive return on Investment might be 
difficult to implement. For technologies to gain attraction in the industry, they need to be 
useful and efficient, proving their value before being widely adopted [67]. 
Bygherreforeningen believes that even though the implementation of advanced technology 
would cost money, this money could be reobtained in reduction of accidents with absence 
from work. So in the long run, they believe that it would definitely be worth it despite the 
costs [60]. 
Dansk Industri also thinks that the construction industry is slow in adoption of new 
technologies due to the small profits they operate at [68]. 
 
==PAGE:48==
Page 47 of 246 
 
Which complications do you think could occur with the implementation of this advanced 
technology? 
3F have already answered this in previous questions. They are mainly concerned about the 
General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) and the workers' opinion about being monitored 
[67]. 
Bygherreforeningen believe that some of people could have concerns about the monitoring 
aspects of it. But most workers already have a mobile phone which records their location 
whether they want it or not, and no one thinks about that. Based on that, 
Bygherreforeningen believes that it is an illusion to think that you are not already being 
monitored. So, if the monitoring could help ensure the safety of workers, then it should not 
be a problem [60]. 
Dansk Industri already had answered this question in a previous question. There are 
concerns that workers might feel like they are under surveillance constantly and there might 
be a misuse of the data from the employers’ side [68]. 
 
Can this complication be overcome? 
- if yes, how so? 
3F states that if the technology is used ethically correct and the data does not impose 
extensive requirements on how to handle collected data, then it should not be a problem 
[67]. 
Bygherreforeningen already had answered this question in the previous question. If you can 
present and explain it correctly and mention that the monitoring is done for their own good, 
then this complication could be overcome [60]. 
Dansk Industri believes that it depends on how the data is handled and how the concept is 
presented and explained [68]. 
 
Rental Companies 
Can you tell us a little bit about who you guys are, and what you do? What types of 
machines do you rent out? 
GSV rents out everything from small equipment to big excavators. They call themselves a 
one stop shop, so if their customers need something that GSV does not own, they rent it for 
their customers. All the items that they rent out is something that they buy, they do not 
produce it themselves, but they have a close collaboration with the producers, so that they 
can affect the production if the need arises [62]. 
Loxam rents out every machinery that is related to the construction industry. Everything 
from smaller machines to big terrain vehicles. They are not just based in Denmark but have 
a global presence too [64]. 
==PAGE:49==
Page 48 of 246 
 
What kind of companies do you primarily rent out to? 
GSV’s primary customers are big contractor companies such as Per Aarsleff and Barslund 
[62]. 
Loxam’s customers vary widely from very small private contractor firms to much bigger 
contractors [64]. 
 
Do you think that’s accidents on construction sites happen often, and is still a major 
problem? 
GSV believes that accidents is still something that happens very often and is an actual 
problem, based on what they hear from their customers [62]. 
Loxam believes that accidents happen very frequently and is still a big problem, as they 
sometimes in rare cases can lead to death, which is very serious and unacceptable [64]. 
 
What types of accidents do you experience, or have you heard of, happens most on 
construction sites? 
The majority of accidents that GSV hears of are wiggling of the foot, cutting with a knife, 
stumbling and stepping wrongly into a hole for example [62]. 
Loxam did not have a clear answer to this question, as they are not directly involved in the 
accidents, neither are they notified about accidents unless one of their vehicles had been 
involved. 
 
Do you think that accidents where vehicles or cranes are involved, is something that happens 
often, and is a major problem? 
GSV does not believe that vehicle accidents are something that happens often. It belongs to 
the rare category and is something that very seldom happens [62]. 
This question was not asked to Loxam since it was not relevant based on their answer to the 
previous question. 
 
Do you guys do anything from your side to prevent accidents and improve the safety on 
construction sites? 
- If yes, what do you do? 
GSV has implemented several approaches in order to reduce the number of accidents on 
construction sites. This includes video instructions, instruction requirements, safety 
campaigns, an app to report risk observations and a modification of their hiring process [62]. 
Loxam has an information obligation where they must instruct their customers on how to 
use the equipment and vehicles they rent out, in a way that is safe [64]. 
 
==PAGE:50==
Page 49 of 246 
 
What are your opinions on the implementation of advanced technology, such as location-
based GPS sensors and cameras worn by workers and installed in vehicles, as a tool to 
improve the safety on construction sites and to prevent of accidents? 
GSV has a positive opinion about the concept. They have done an effort into digitalization 
themselves and believes that everything that relates to technology is positive if it can 
improve the safety on construction sites without being a nuisance for the workers [62]. 
Loxam has a 100% positive opinion about the concept. The more optimization can be done 
in regard to safety on construction sites, the better [64]. 
 
What do you think your customers’ opinions on this would be? 
GSV believes that if as long as the implementation of the concept is done correctly in regard 
to law and permissions, they believe that the affected workers would have a positive stance 
towards it [62]. 
Loxam believes that it is possible that some of the customers would not be too happy about 
because of the subject of monitoring. They also believe that if the goal is to improve the 
safety of the affected workers, then it should not be a problem [64]. 
 
Do you think that the implementation of this technology realistically could improve the 
safety on construction sites? 
GSV is in doubt about whether the concept would actually be effective, since the technology 
would not improve upon the types of accidents that they mostly hear about. But on other 
construction sites where the types of accidents differ and vehicle related accidents are more 
prominent, the interviewee believes that it could have a positive effect on the prevention of 
these vehicle related accidents [62]. 
Loxam believes that by adding more technology, it could reduce the chances of vehicle 
related accidents even further [64]. 
 
Do you think that the implementation of this technology will be worth it in spite of the 
expenses that could occur with the installation and maintenance of these technologies? 
GSV believes that it is hard to give an answer, when they do not yet know how much the 
implementation of this technology would cost. On the other hand, they say that safety 
cannot be measured in money. If it realistically can help improve the safety on construction 
sites and prevent accidents, then money should not be a question [62]. 
Loxam believes that is definitely worth it to pay a little extra for an improved safety and the 
potential of reducing the number of accidents that can happen [64]. 
==PAGE:51==
Page 50 of 246 
 
Which complications do you think could occur with the implementation of this advanced 
technology? 
GSV believes that some of the complications that could occur are law and permissions, and 
the fact that technology must be an inconvenience for workers [62]. 
Loxam believes that some of the complications that could happen would be GDPR and the 
feeling of the workers feeling monitored [64]. 
 
Can this complication be overcome? 
- if yes, how so? 
GSV believes that it is all about how you sell the idea. They believe that it would beg the 
question of monitoring from some people, but on the other hand most people already have 
a phone with localization and tracking capabilities. If the concept is presented in this way, 
and it is explained to the workers why they have to be monitored and how it would 
positively affect their own safety, then they believe that the questions could be overcome 
[62]. 
Loxam suggests that a point could be made about that the monitoring would only be there 
to improve the work environment of the affected workers [64]. 
 
Would you consider installing the aforementioned technologies on your vehicles and 
machines if it could improve the safety on construction sites? 
GSV believes that even if the vehicle related accidents are low, they would still be open to 
consider the implementation of this concept, if it means even more safety for the workers 
[62]. 
Based on the previous question, Loxam would very much consider to install the technologies 
if it would mean improving the safety on construction sites and preventing vehicle related 
accidents.

Algorithms 
This section serves to present the finished algorithm prototypes, how they work, how to use 
them, and shows an example of them being used. 
As already mentioned, two algorithms have been created and both have been transformed 
into executable files. This means that the programs can be run from any pc, without the 
need to download additional requirements. These programs can be seen on appendices 23 
and 24. 
The programs serve as an after-the-fact tool, that allows users to process the data output 
from RTK-GNSS systems in a fast and efficient manner and translates the raw data into a 
more comprehensible language. This data can then be used to support decisions and actions 
in relation to improving safety on construction sites. 
The first algorithm serves to investigate a data set and show every time a worker was within 
a specified distance to a vehicle. The raw code behind this algorithm can be seen in 
appendix 25. 
The second algorithm investigates every time a worker walked into a pre-specified 
dangerous zone. The raw code behind this algorithm can be seen in appendix 26. 
Both algorithms use the same raw data set. As already mentioned in the methods section, 
this data set was the only one available to us. A snapshot of the data set that has been used 
can be seen below, in order to understand the raw data set in its raw format. 
 
Figure 11: A snapshot showing the raw data set from RTK-GNSS. 
As can be seen on the figure, each line represents a data entry from a tag. The data entries 
consist of ID’s, which in the case of this data set is WORKER_A, WORKER_B, WORKER_C and 
ZEMENTMISCHER_A (Concrete truck), latitudes, longitudes, altitudes, and date. Based on 
that information, it can be seen that the data set consists of 4 tags recording their positions 
==PAGE:54==
Page 53 of 246 
 
simultaneously for every second. These inputs are separated by a semicolon (;). Therefor 
the algorithm is made in a way so it recognizes the semicolons as separators. 
Examples and explanations of both algorithms will be shown in the subsections below. 
 
Example of algorithm 1 – Proximity detection 
The program will need a data set from an RTK-GNSS system to function, so the total amount 
of required files for the algorithm to run successfully is 2 files, which the figure below also 
depicts. 
 
Figure 12: A view of the standalone program and the data set. 
By launching the program ”Proximitydetection.exe” the user is greeted by a small popup 
window, with 2 fillable fields and 1 field where a file can be chosen. The first field serves to 
rename the ID “ZEMENTMISCHER_A” into whatever is input, while the second field 
determines what distance the proximity analysis should investigate for (Figure 13). 
 
Figure 13: Popup window upon launch with 2 fillable fields and one field where a file can be chosen. 
For this example, the name “Concrete Truck” and a proximity distance of 6 meters will be 
used (Figure 14). This will rename the ID “ZEMENTMISCHER_A” into “Concrete Truck”, and 
the algorithm will search and find every time a worker was within 6 meters of the concrete 
truck.  
==PAGE:55==
Page 54 of 246 
 
 
Figure 14: Popup window with fields filled out, with “concrete truck” and “6”. 
This is done by assigning the ID’s starting with “WORKER” into one list, and the concrete 
truck into another list. The lists are then compared to each other and the results with a 
proximity distance of 0 to 6 meters within the same timestamp, are isolated and shown. 
This happens very fast, and the results are given almost instantly (Figure 15).  
 
Figure 15: A window showing the found results after data processing is complete. 
The results are shown in a separate window as can be seen on Figure 15. The results in this 
case consists of 16 found incidents, where each incident is listed with the name of the 
worker and vehicle involved, and the time of occurrence. Simultaneously a folder is 
generated which is shown and highlighted on Figure 16. This folder is created in the same 
directory as the executable file, to make is easy for the user to locate. 
==PAGE:56==
Page 55 of 246 
 
 
Figure 16: Directory of the program with the newly generated folder highlighted. 
Inside the folder (Figure 17), a summary of the results shown on Figure 16, is saved in a .txt 
file. Furthermore, for each found incident a file is created that visually shows the incident, 
which makes the results very comprehensible and easy to understand. The files contain the 
affected worker and vehicle ID’s and timestamps in the name, to give a better overview and 
make it easy for the user to locate and open a specific incident. 
 
Figure 17: Contents of the newly generated folder. 
By opening one of the visualization files, a satellite view is shown of the corresponding place 
where the incident took place (Figure 18). The files are interactable satellite views, which 
means that it is not merely a picture but an actual map that can be moved around and 
zooming in or out is possible. The view shows the affected worker and vehicle with a red 
colour, while the other workers outside the proximity zone are shown with a blue colour. A 
red circle can also be seen around the vehicle’s location. This circle is the proximity zone and 
is dynamic, which means that the radius of the circle will always be equal to the input 
distance being investigated for. In the case of this example, the radius is 6 meters. 
==PAGE:57==
Page 56 of 246 
 
 
Figure 18: Visualization of one of the incidents found, with the affected worker highlighted with a red colour. 
 
Example of algorithm 2 – Dangerous zones detection 
This program also needs a data set from an RTK-GNSS system to function, so the total 
amount of required files for the algorithm to run successfully is 2 files, which the figure 
below also depicts. 
 
Figure 19: A view of the standalone program and a data set 
When launching the program ”Dangerouszones.exe” the user is also greeted with 
preliminary popup window, this time with a field where the data set can be chosen from the 
directory and a set of fields for inputting latitude and longitude values. Additionally, when 
clicking the button “Add row of coordinates” a new row of fields for coordinates will be 
added (Figure 20). 
==PAGE:58==
Page 57 of 246 
 
 
Figure 20: Preliminary popup window where the data set can be chosen and coordinates can be input. 
For the purpose of this example, the same data set has been used, and the “Add row of 
coordinates” button has been pressed 3 times, to be able to input 4 sets of coordinates. 
These random test coordinates have been chosen because they are within the confines of 
the data set and can be seen on Figure 21.  
In real practice these coordinates will define the corners of the dangerous zone that the 
user wishes to investigate for. This will require some preparation as the user will need to go 
out on the construction site with some kind of localization sensor to measure and determine 
the coordinates for the corners of the dangerous zone that the user wishes to investigate 
for. The RTK-GNSS or another sensor could be used for this. If an updated satellite image on 
for example google maps exists of the construction site, the physical aspect of going out on 
the construction site can thus be bypassed, as the coordinates could be derived from google 
maps. 
 
Figure 21: Example of preliminary popup window with the fields filled. 
The algorithm will now form a polygon based on the input coordinates, in this case a square, 
and will detect every time a worker ID entered the dangerous zone. These results are then 
isolated and shown, almost instantly when clicking the “OK” button (Figure 22). 
==PAGE:59==
Page 58 of 246 
 
 
Figure 22: A window showing the found results after the algorithm has finished processing the data. 
The results are shown in a separate popup window as can be seen on Figure 22. In the case 
of this example, 25 incidents have been found, where each is listed with the involved 
workers’ ID, time of occurrence and coordinates of the location where the incident took 
place.  
Simultaneously a folder is also created with this algorithm which is shown and highlighted 
on Figure 23. This folder is also created in the same directory as the executable file for easy 
location. 
 
Figure 23: Directory of the program with the newly generated folder highlighted. 
Inside the folder (Figure 24), a summary of the results shown in the popup window on 
Figure 22 are saved as a .txt file. Additionally, for each found incident, two files are created 
that visually show the incidents. The files contain the involved workers’ ID and time of 
occurrence in the file name. Like the previous algorithm, this is done give a better overview, 
and make it easy for the user to locate a specific incident. 
==PAGE:60==
Page 59 of 246 
 
 
Figure 24: Contents of the newly created folder. Not all results for the example are shown in the snapshot. 
By opening the first of the two generated files for each incident, a satellite view is shown in 
the user’s browser, which visualizes the incident (Figure 25). This algorithm also produces 
interactable files which can be moved around and zooming in or out is possible.  
The view shows a visual representation of the pre-defined danger zone created from the 
input coordinates in Figure 21, in red and an icon for the affected worker, which in this case 
is the position of WORKER_C when that worker trespassed into the dangerous zone. 
 
Figure 25: Visual representation of an example incident. 
When opening the second of the two generated files for each incident, a similar satellite 
view is shown (Figure 26).  
The view shows the same incident, but instead of a stationary position for the involved 
worker, a trajectory instead is shown with a blue line. This trajectory starts 20 seconds 
before the time of occurrence and ends 20 seconds after the time of occurrence. 
Additionally, an icon with the name “start” is also generated to define the start of the 
trajectory, as without it, it would be hard to determine the direction of the trajectory, as 
this is just shown as a blue line. 
==PAGE:61==
Page 60 of 246 
 
 
Figure 26: Visual representation of the same incident, with trajectory shown. 
The purpose of showing the 20 seconds before and after the incident with a trajectory line is 
to visually show where the worker was coming from and where the worker was headed to, 
when that worker entered the dangerous zone. This could help the user spot a pattern in 
terms of specific paths causing the workers to enter dangerous zones and could support a 
potential pro-active action to avoid this in the future. 
 
 
==PAGE:62==
Page 61 of 246 
 
Discussion 
Opinions on implementation of advanced technologies on construction sites 
Location-based technology is a topic that has been academically explored and proven to 
have positive results. Yet there is a lack of adaptation in real construction projects. Opinions 
from construction stakeholders play an important role in the process of adoption. 
Furthermore, the perceptions of construction managers and the acceptance of construction 
workers toward location-based technologies is also important factors [28]. 
The decision process for adaptation of new technology in any industry is affected by the 
high-ranking managers, and this includes the construction industry. Several factors can 
influence the managers’ decision process. Lack of general awareness or inadequate 
understanding of how the technologies work or their potential value, may result in them 
being hesitant to adopt it. Education and training initiatives can help address the resistance 
to change by providing the necessary knowledge. Managers need to have a broad 
understanding of the benefits and capabilities of the new technologies. This allows them to 
make informed decisions and evaluate how the technology can improve their operations 
productivity and safety of workers  [28]. 
This correlates with what Campus Service expressed during the interviews. They believe that 
in order for the concept of using advanced technologies to monitor the locations of the 
workers on construction sites to be realized, it should be introduced by a high-ranking actor 
which in this case would be the project owner. If the project owners set it as a requirement, 
the following bidding contractors and subcontractors have no choice but to abide by this 
requirement if they want to bid on the project. If the concept  and the reasoning is 
explained thoroughly and the usefulness and advantages of the data the concept produces 
is presented correctly and it is explained that the concept would merely be a measure to 
improve safety on construction sites then Campus Service believes that the concept would 
have a higher chance of successful implementation during the construction phase of a 
project, compared to a direct approach towards a contractor [49].  
This was even further confirmed when the contractors were asked about their opinions on 
the concept during the interviews. 3 out of the 4 asked contractors, did either not deem the 
implementation of the concept necessary or had not given it any thought [51] [54] [57]. 
They did not see any reason for the concept and could not see what good it would do. They 
believe that they should have planned their work in a way that makes the concept useless 
[51] [57]. This supports Campus Service’s statement about the concept having a higher 
chance of successful implementation if it starts with the project owner. 
Before implementing new technologies, employees are consulted, although managerial 
support affects employees’ intentions to accept a new system. Studies have been conducted 
about the acceptance of construction workers towards different technologies such as IT, 
Building information modelling (BIM) , mobile computing devices and wearable technologies 
[69] [70]. The studies highlight that privacy, security and confidentiality is a key 
consideration among workers towards particularly on wearable technologies, which also 
was some of the concerns of the companies interviewed in this study. 1 of the 2 project 
==PAGE:63==
Page 62 of 246 
 
owners, 2 of the 4 contractors, 1 of the 2 rental companies and all 3 unions interviewed all 
expressed concerns that the affected workers who would be wearing the technology would 
feel monitored, which could cause inefficiency and reduce the sense of freedom on the 
construction sites [66] [54] [55] [64] [67] [60] [68]. 
However, workers are more likely to be more agreeable to the use the wearable 
technologies if the collected data only occurs during working hours. The motivation for 
construction workers to wear these technologies are the benefits of their health and safety 
that the wearable technology would provide [28].  
NCC also expressed that by making the data collected from the RTK-GNSS anonymous and 
use the data to detect certain patterns and overall movement that could potentially lead to 
accidents, instead of using it as a tool to investigate specific individual workers, the concept 
would have a higher chance of successful implementation and would lead to the workers 
being more inclined to accept the implementation of the concept in practice [55]. 
Despite this, the general opinion on the implementation of the concept with advanced 
technologies with monitoring capabilities is not solely negative. Both the interviewed 
project owners, 1 of the 4 contractors, all rental companies, and all unions, have a positive 
opinion about the concept. They can see the advantages and the useful data the concept 
could provide and believe that with a successful implementation it could realistically end up 
improving the safety on construction sites and reducing the number of accidents [49] [66] 
[55] [62] [64] [67] [60] [68]. The successful implementation entails that the monitoring 
aspect would be dealt with by making the data anonymous and the project owners 
enforcing it as a requirement for potential bidders [49] [55]. 
 
Complications and limitations 
General Data Protection Regulation - GDPR 
While location-based sensors can improve safety on construction sites by collecting a vast 
amount of data of real time monitoring, ethical considerations should be given regarding 
personal data and monitoring of employees, as it might bring some challenges when 
adapting the technologies in Danish organizations and organizations in Europe generally, 
since construction companies need to follow the General Data protection Regulation 
(GDPR). GDPR is a comprehensive data protection and privacy regulation implemented by 
the European Union (EU) where Denmark was included in 2018 [71]. 
GDPR was also a concern with several of the interviewed companies, regarding the 
implementation of location-based sensors. GSV, Loxam, 3F and Dansk Industri all admitted 
that GDPR would be one of the major complications on the road to implementing the 
concept [62] [64] [67] [68]. 3F and Dansk Industri both mention that the reason for the 
importance of GDPR is to prevent misuse of the generated data from the location-based 
systems. A potential misuse of the data could be managers and employers using the data as 
a surveillance tool to keep an eye on the employees on the job and could result in the 
employees feeling like prisoners or even resulting in an increase of firing rates as a direct 
==PAGE:64==
Page 63 of 246 
 
result of the implementation of the concept. That is why GDPR is in place, to prevent this 
kind of misuse of personal data, and to ensure that the collected data is handled correctly 
[67] [68]. 
The GDPR introduces several key principles and rights. Firstly, Organizations must have a 
lawful basis for processing personal data of workers. That means that the organizations 
must give a valid explanation of the purpose for collecting and processing the data and be 
transparent on how it’s done. In this case it is for the improvement of health and safety of 
construction workers to reduce the number of accidents and close calls on site. As 
mentioned in the previous section, workers are more inclined to use the wearable 
technologies if it is for the benefit of their own safety. 
Secondly the individual workers must give their consent for the processing of their personal 
data, and they have the right to withdraw their consent at any time. It’s important that 
workers are aware of the methods and their rights. That can include the right to access their 
data, and object to certain types of processing. As mentioned in the previous section, 
workers are more agreeable for data to be collected under certain circumstances like 
working hours, but also cautious about how the gathered information is used. For instance, 
if the performance of the individual worker was monitored it could be used as a tool to root 
out inefficient workers, which would be a misuse of the intended use of the concept, as 
already mentioned. 
Organizations are accountable for their data protection practices. They are required to 
implement suitable technical measurements to ensure the security and protection of 
personal data. Furthermore, they need to maintain documentation to prove their 
compliance with GDPR requirements, which promotes a culture of accountability and 
transparency. 
Lastly, in the event of a data breach that could lead to a potential risk of individuals' rights 
and freedoms. The organization are obligated to notify the affected individuals and relevant 
supervisory authority within a specific time frame, to ensure that appropriate actions are 
taken to minimize the impact damage and safeguard the individual’s personal data. 
 
Cost and economy 
The cost is another limitation when implementing and maintaining the location-based 
advanced technology. It will require an initial investment in purchasing and installing the 
systems and devices as well as integrating them with the existing safety measures and 
safety equipment. There may also be extra costs relating to calibration and maintenance. 
These factors can be a significant barrier to the implementation of these technologies 
specifically for smaller companies or organizations that work on a tight budget.  Which also 
was a concern of most of the companies interviewed in this study. Campus Service, 
Hovedstadens Letbane, GSV, 3F and Dansk Industri all acknowledged that the cost is a major 
consideration and limitation in regards to the implementation of the concept [49] [66] [62] 
[67] [68].  
==PAGE:65==
Page 64 of 246 
 
Hovedstadens Letbane believe that cost is a dilemma. If a concept can improve the safety of 
workers on construction sites, then the cost is worth it. But on the other hand, a balance 
must be maintained because economy and time schedules are very important aspects and 
affects the success of a construction project [66]. 
Campus Service agrees with the statement above and expresses that the price for 
implementation must not be too high. At some point the when the cost becomes too high, it 
might not be worth it any longer [49]. 
GSV expressed that it is hard to give an answer about their stance on the costs, without 
knowing the exact costs the implementation of the concept would entail. On the other 
hand, they expressed that safety cannot be measured in money and that it should not be a 
question if the concept would actually work [62]. But the fact that they did not immediately 
give an answer is an indicator of the costs also having an influence on their willingness to 
implement the concept. 
Both 3F and Dansk Industri present some concerns regarding the cost of the 
implementation. The construction industry in general does not generate a lot of profit, 
which is why the implementation of technology that cost money would entail economic 
complications, if it does not immediately return a profit [67] [68]. Bygherreforeningen takes 
a different stance on the matter. They believe that the cost is worth it, as the 
implementation would regain that lost money in the long run when accounting for the 
reduction of accidents, which in turn reduces the number of sick leaves and absence from 
work [60]. 
A preliminary estimate of the costs with setting up RTK-GNSS systems is 1000-1500 Euro per 
setup. This is an estimate, given by Professor Jochen Teizer at DTU. 
 
Physical size and setup 
Despite the usefulness and the centimeter-level accuracy of the RTK-GNSS systems, the 
technology comes with a downside regarding the physical setup. The system consists of a 
box receiver, a board with an antenna, and a special phone. This 3-part setup is relatively big 
and would be complicated to find a wearable solution for, which correlates with some of the 
interviewee’s concerns about size and inconvenience. 
Both Campus Service and NCC expressed concerns regarding that if the technology was too 
big and complex to wear, it could cause potential complications for the successful 
implementation of the concept [49] [55]. They both believe that if the implementation 
should be a success, the affected workers must be free of any additional responsibility and 
inconvenience that could be caused as a result of the concept. 
As of this moment, there is no going around the physical size and complex setup, but at 
some point, in the future the technology will have been optimized enough for size and 
convenience.  
==PAGE:66==
Page 65 of 246 
 
Another suggestion would be to integrate the technology into a safety vest, which would 
make it easier and more convenient to wear. 
A third alternative would be to use alternatives to the RTK-GNSS systems. These can include 
Bluetooth Low Energy tags, GNSS tags, RFID tags or Ultra-Wideband tags. These options do 
have some downsides which includes low accuracy and precision due to distance 
degradation. Some of these also require static anchor nodes to be set up in advance which 
can prove costly and time consuming, but also require direct line of sight from the 
transponder tags to the receiver nodes for accurate readings, which is not always possible 
on a construction site [72]. This is where the RTK-GNSS systems have an advantage. They do 
not require anchor nodes set up as they directly use satellites for trilateration and a base 
station for correctional adjustments. 
 
Algorithm related limitations 
The algorithms used for data processing also present some limitations of their own. One of 
these limitations that could cause some difficulties for some users, is that the second 
algorithm requires a set of coordinates to be input in order to define the danger zone. This 
would mean that the user already needs to know the precise coordinates that make up the 
boundaries of the danger zone they wish to investigate or be willing to go out on the 
construction site and manually measure and get the coordinates with a GNSS tool. This also 
presents another problem regarding accuracy, depending on what tool is used for this. 
Another limitation regarding the input coordinates is that due to the nature of the 
algorithm, the coordinates must be input in a specific order, either clockwise or 
counterclockwise. Failure to do this will result in the algorithm drawing wrong shapes from 
the coordinates. 
Another limitation is that the algorithms were designed to be an after-the-fact tool, to 
analyze close encounters and accidents after they already have happened. This might 
present some limitations for some people and companies, if they deem the algorithms 
worthless since they do not have any real-time interaction. 
The algorithm was intended to be made universal and able to work with every single 
possible GNSS data. But since it was designed after one specific data set, additional 
modification of the algorithms and additional data sets are needed in order to make the 
algorithms fully universal. 
 
Anticipated results and impacts with the concept 
 
There are many different types of accidents occurring on construction sites today. Due to 
the wide variety of these, the concept of location-based technology will only be able to 
positively influence a selection of them.  
Based on the interviewees’ answers, the most often occurring accidents and close 
encounters are falls [66] [54] [55] [57] [62] [67] [60] [68], cutting accidents [49] [54] [55] 
==PAGE:67==
Page 66 of 246 
 
[57] [62] [60] [68], twisting of ankles [49] [57] [62], physical overload [66] [68], falling 
objects [66], willingness of taking risks [51], ventures into dangerous zones [49], vehicle 
collisions [66] [67], overturned vehicles [66] [51] [60] and crane related incidents [49] [54] 
[55]. 
Falls, stumbling and twisting of ankles are often results of improper cleaning and loose 
objects lying about or walking in fresh excavated areas [55] [57]. Other causes of falls is the 
difference of elevations on construction sites and workers carrying objects with reduces 
their field of view [67]. 
Physical overload is often the result of workers doing the same repetitive tasks repeatedly 
[68]. 
The willingness of taking risks can be a result of workers forgetting their PPE equipment and 
being too lazy to go back to get it or taking a shortcut instead of doing an action the proper 
and safe way [51]. 
Vehicle collisions often happen on construction sites adjacent to heavy traffic and the 
public. Because of the small size of the construction sites, vehicle collisions have a higher 
chance of taking place [66]. 
Overturned vehicles can happen when a truck arrives on the construction site outside of 
working hours and thus no one is available to guide them, which leads them to off-load on 
uneven ground, resulting in overturning. In cases where the truckdriver gets severely hurt, 
there is no one on-site to help them [60]. 
Crane related incidents are results of workers not being mindful about not walking 
underneath airborne loads that the crane is in the process of moving, and the load suddenly 
comes loose and crashes [49]. 
The concept is not relevant to the majority of these types of accidents such as falls, cutting 
accidents, twisting of ankles, physical overload, falling of objects and overturned vehicles, 
since the implementation would not have a direct impact on these accidents and therefore 
would not reduce these types of accidents. 
But the concept could potentially reduce the other types of accidents, which include 
willingness of taking risks, vehicle collisions, venturing into dangerous zones and crane 
related incidents. The feeling of being monitored could in this case be turned into a positive 
thing, since the workers feeling monitored would rethink taking unnecessary and 
spontaneous risks, which in turn would reduce the number of accidents that are a result of 
these unnecessary risks. 
Vehicle collisions can also be reduced by using the location-based technology in conjunction 
with the first algorithm to analyse the close call encounters and take pro-active actions to 
prevent these. 
Likewise, the location-based technology would in conjunction with the second algorithm be 
able to reduce the number of incidents related to dangerous zones and workers walking 
==PAGE:68==
Page 67 of 246 
 
under crane liftings, by investigating if people are venturing into these dangerous zones and 
taking actions accordingly. 
The concept would also ensure that all incidents and close call encounters would be 
detected and reported, since it would no longer rely on manual registering and reporting 
from the individual workers but would be supported by hard evidence from the processed 
data. 
The concept would therefore not have any effect on the most common types of accidents, 
but it would be able to improve on other types of accidents, which would still be a 
significant improvement of the safety on construction sites. 
 
 
==PAGE:69==
Page 68 of 246 
 
Conclusion and future work  
Many different types of accidents and close calls happen today on construction sites in 
Denmark. These incidents are of a very wide variety, and the concept with implementing 
location-based technology for tracking and algorithms for data processing, might not 
positively affect the most frequently occurring accidents and close calls, such as falls, cutting 
and physical overload. 
The concept focuses instead on specific accidents that have a lower frequency, however 
despite their lower frequency, these accidents have a higher chance of fatal and 
catastrophic consequences that can result in deaths, compared to the accidents with higher 
occurrence. These accidents include vehicle collisions, dangerous zones, and crane related 
accidents, which the concept could potentially combat, by analyzing dangerous patterns of 
the workers and acting before these close calls become full-fledged accidents. 
The concept also does not send out live alerts when an accident is about to happen. The 
concept is merely intended as an after-the-fact tool to help managers and safety 
coordinators analyze patterns on the construction site and is therefore not intended to be 
used as a standalone tool, but rather as a support tool to already existing safety measures. 
The general opinion of the implementation of the concept based on the conducted 
interviews was mostly positive. In fact, 72% of the interviewed companies believe that the 
concept could have a positive impact and it was clear to them the potential the concept 
would have, and the amount of useful data it would produce. The remaining 3 companies 
who did not have a positive opinion on the concept were all contractors which is a point 
worth noting, since the contractors would play a major role in enforcing the concept. But if 
project owners made the concept a requirement, the bidding contractors would have no 
choice but to comply with the concept if they wish to bid for the projects. 
Despite the positive general opinions, there are some concerns and complications with 
implementing the concept. These include GDPR, costs and physical size. 
Some of the complications can be overcome by making the generated data anonymous and 
by using the tool to investigate patterns instead of individual workers. 
This project and the concept is a preliminary attempt at incorporating RTK-GNSS systems 
into the construction sites as a safety measure, and thus there is room for improvement and 
possibilities for future work, which will be mentioned below. 
By having the possibility to use RTK-GNSS systems to test and record data firsthand, it could 
be easier to determine whether the concept would be reliable and work, and other 
potential challenges could appear, which can then be handled. By having primary sources of 
data, it would also allow a person to modify the algorithm to be universal and in that way be 
able to work with every single possible generated data from RTK-GNSS systems. 
Another possibility for future work would be to interview actual workers that directly work 
on the construction sites, since it was not possible to do so during this project. Having 
==PAGE:70==
Page 69 of 246 
 
opinions from these workers would be highly relevant and productive, since the workers are 
the ones directly affected by the implementation of wearable location-based technologies. 
After reaching the end of this project, it can be concluded that RTK-GNSS systems in 
conjunction with the prototype algorithms would theoretically have a positive effect on 
safety on construction sites, by producing valuable and important close call data, which 
would support safety managers in their decisions. The success of the concept entails that 
the data is made anonymous and that the managers and those responsible for the 
implementation comply with the GDPR requirements.

Appendix 4 – Enemærke & Pedersen interview transcription 
Jeg prøver at køre derudad. Ja men altså. Lidt et oplæg om jamen hvem er vi? Egentlig 
mærker Petersen og og. Hvad? Hvem er? Vi i Vores. Arbejdsmiljø afdeling og hvordan 
arbejder vi med vi med arbejdsmiljøet? Det er Sådan. Set det vi prøver at gennemgå her. Og 
Det er jo lidt i forhold til jamen. Vi har jo været noget, der hedder flere forskellige Erhverv 
nu forretningsområder, og man kan sige det det vi nok er mest kendt for. Det er Det er 
renovering af alment nyttigt boligbyggeri. Og og så kan man sige, jamen, Vi har. Vi har en del 
i forhold til det almindelige licitations marked, men så har vi også Vores strategiske 
partnerskaber, hvor, hvor Vi har nogle samarbejdspartnere i forhold til. Til for eksempel 
nogle boligselskaber og Københavns Kommune, som vi kommer ind på senere. Og så har vi 
noget projektudvikling, vi laver. Vi har for eksempel noget på kyst, hvor vi laver et kæmpe 
nybyggeri i samarbejde med pension Danmark. Et projekt til 1,2 milliarder. Så har vi hvad 
det nu hedder 2 datterselskaber også det der hedder ravnstrup og nemt bygge og hvis man 
ser fra landkort derovre, så kan man jo se alle de lokationer hvor Der er en med blåt. Det er 
ravnstrup sø lokationer og en mærker Petersen lige så repræsenteret 4 steder i Danmark. I 
Brabrand ved Århus og hovedsæde her i Ringsted eller nogle barrierer på Fyn men. Men der 
har vi en afdeling i Odense, og så har vi hovedsæde der i Ringsted, og så har vi Vores bygge 
fabrik i Glostrup, hvor vi laver præfabrikerede træelementer blandt andet og og 
tagkassetter. Det er 700 medarbejdere i enemærke og Petersen plus 300 i Vores 
datterselskaber, og Vi har en omsætning på 2,3 milliarder i enemærke og Petersen alene og 
tilsammen med Vores datter vil skabe cirka 3,3 milliarder. Jamen Der er lidt i forhold til hvor 
vi hvor Vi er bosat hjemme og og Der er også, hvor Vi har Vores projektkontor i de der 
strategiske partnerskaber, og man kan sige, jamen Sådan i gennemsnit og året rundt. Der 
har vi cirka 50 aktive byggepladser på landsplan. 
OK. 
Hvad er de her strategiske partnerskaber, som som Vi er, hvor det Vi har det her trust det 
samarbejde med Københavns Kommune, vi vi renoverer rigtig mange skoler. Verdener der 
hedder. For for Københavns Kommune og det her samarbejde. Det er så med med sved sko, 
dominia krav og berget norconsult lyt nord sigsgaard. Og så er der det her partnerskab, der 
hedder over os, som som er en del af af Københavns boligselskab KB. Og så har vi igen på. 
Fyn, hvor Vi har. Et boligselskab noget der hedder liva. Og Vi har Sådan et partnerskab på, 
hvor vi egentlig det, der egentlig er for partnerskaberne. Det er jo egentlig hvor vi. Vi laver 
nogle. Rammeaftaler med med de her bygherrer omkring i totalentreprise. Og så kan man 
sige, at man arbejder med åbne bøger i forhold til, at man. Den måde man man bygger på, 
at at man egentlig arbejder med, at man gerne vil have et dækningsbidrag på et eller andet. 
Jamen selv procent, og så er jeg. Så prøver man egentlig sammen og finde de de bedste 
løsninger i fællesskab med. Med med rådgivere og bygherrer, så så man kan sige at og det 
det gode ved de der partnerskaber. Det er jo også at, at når vi vi egentlig har er 
kontraktholder med med bygherre, og vi hylder Vores egne rådgivere, jamen, så er det jo. 
Man kan sige, jamen så har. Vi også mulighed for. At påvirke det rent arbejdsmiljømæssigt 
at at. At vi i sidste. Ende får en plan for sikkerhed og sundhed, og vi får nogle 
arbejdsbeskrivelser, som som er gode og varetager det gode arbejdsmiljø. Kan man sige. 
Jamen, så er der jo egentlig også i arbejdsfordeling, hvis man starter med. Men dagen i

midten. Det er Vores arbejdsmiljøchef Rikke kirkebjerg. Og til Venstre i billedet er det min

nogle ting der der mangler at blive taget prøver i forhold til nogle byggematerialer, hvor der

Miljørapporten og så. 
Ja ja. 
Men Det er Sådan meget det jeg så så er det her. Det er Sådan set, hvordan vi organiseret i

Vores arbejdsmiljø, udvalgsmøder og så videre. Og Vi er. Jo, Vi er jo også 
arbejdsmiljøcertificeret. Det glemmer det måske at fortælle og der. Har vi jo egentlig. Der 
har vi. Jo togange årligt verden noget der hedder intern. 
Årligt hvor vi hvor vi.

Page 139 of 246 
 
Har et repræsentativt udvalg af Vores byggepladser. Hvor vi går. Byggepladsen igennem i 
forhold. Det om, om Vi er enige overholder det her ledelses. Sten, som som Vi har sagt ja til 
en gang, da de var arbejdsmiljøcertificeret altså. Går ud og kigger. På byggepladserne i 
forhold til om, om sikkerheden er i orden, og også for at se, hvordan Vores byggeledelse 
ikke mindst agere derude om om når vi går rundt med dem derude, om de er proaktive om 
de om de standser og underentreprenører, hvis Der er et eller andet, der Der er på vej til at 
blive farligt, eller man ser, at Der er nogle mangler ude på byggepladsen, at at ligesom at de 
leder arbejdsmiljøet også derude. Så har vi jo. Egentlig Vi har. Det her skærmprint. Det er 
Sådan set taget fra Vores intra hvor man kan se jamen jamen. Det her det. Er lidt i forhold til 
der kan man altid gå ind og se hvor mange ulykker Vi har Vi har haft og hvad Vores 
ulykkesfrekvens af den ligger på herovre og på fredagsmøderne. Der har vi som regel nogle. 
Nogle kampagner, vi præsenterer overfor for håndværkerne. Det kan være for eksempel 
Arbejdstilsynet rigtig stort fokus på på stol på Vores byggepladser. Og det kunne være den, 
at vi igennem hvor hvor vi egentlig inviterer Vores håndværkere på byggepladsen ind til 
gratis morgenmad. Og hvor at? Vores byggeledelse både orienterede underentreprenører 
og Vores egen produktion i jamen hvad nytter Det er dig og så ligesom hvad er det nu det

Appendix 8 – Loxam interview transcription 
Herfra yes Det er helt fint. OK ja altså med det her advanced avanceret teknologi. Det er 
Sådan vi tænker primært. Det er, at det vil involvere Sådan noget med lokationsbaseret 
sensorer og gps og så videre og også kamera. Yes 2 sekunder. Der fics yes. Vil du starte med 
at fortælle? Lidt om ja hvem hvem Det er du repræsenterer og hvad i gør. I princippet. 
Ja, jeg, Jeg vil sige, Jeg har repræsenteret uagtsom, som er en. Fransk og virksomhed, som er 
den største udlejningsvirksomhed i Europa. Vi har ikke kun forretninger i Europa, men men 
faktisk i mange år her i verden og Vores Vores kerneforretning. Det er udlejning af alle 
former for materiel til byggeriet, industrien. Eller hvor der nu er behov for. For det materiale 
som Vi har, og. Vi udlejer alt fra fra. Både maskiner nærmest til. Til store terrængående 
køretøjer. Store bomlifte som kan gå højt i vejret, så så Jeg vil sige Vores palette materiel er 
temmelig. Bred og hvad hedder det? Og Der er ingen tvivl om at at. Nogle af de. Her ting 
som. Vi nævner i forhold til jeres. Projekt jamen Det er jo noget af det, som Vi har en dialog 
med. Bogens producenter af materialet, fordi vi i bund og grund også gerne være med til at 
sikre, at de møder, eller at de mennesker, som bruger materialet, ikke kommer galt af sted. 
Producerer ikke selv materiel. Vi kode. Nå det materiel Vi har i Vores udlejningsforretning. 
OK ja. Og så er det simpelthen Der er i. Hvert fald ikke noget. Maskineri, som i ikke har i 
princippet. 
Ja Det kan godt være du kan finde nogle specielle maskiner men. Alt generelt generelle 
måske. Mindre materiel du ser på en byggeplads. Jamen, Det har vi faktisk. 
OK. OK hvordan med kran og så videre er det også inkluderet, eller? 
Ikke ikke grave. Altså hvis du tænker på tårnkraner som står fast monteret. 
Jeg tænker bare Sådan bredt. 
Ja nej kroner. 
Kan være semi mobil og. 
Rammer et kram er ligesom et. Område for sig. Inden for den her industri ikke så kraner er. 
Det er decideret gran firmaer og og mobil firmaer, som som varetager de opgaver. 
OK. 
OK. Ja hvem? Jeg ved ikke om det her. Det er noget du kan oplyse, men hvem udlejer Sådan 
hovedsageligt til er Det er det firmaer der har Sådan et kæmpe anlægsprojekter at gøre, 
eller er det kun Sådan små projekter, eller er det egentlig en blanding af det hele? 
Jeg vil sige det. Vi har Vi har Vi har. De helt store entreprenører som kunder og, og så har vi 
ellers hele paletten ned til til håndværksmesteren, som som kun har sig selv. 
OK. Kunne du måske give et par eksempler på Sådan entreprenørfirmaer, som i udlejer til? 
Men Det kan være Det kan være en. C Det kan være munk. Altså II den års løft. Så så, så Det 
er det helt store. Spillere, som vi samarbejder. Med og så er det jo så. Og så som jeg siger, så 
==PAGE:196==
Page 195 of 246 
 
er det. Så er det helt ned til de til de helt små håndværksmestre. Nu udlejer. Kan man sige. 
Meget lidt til private, men har har en lille smule udlejning der i det segment. 
OK. Synes i hos loxam at ulykker på byggepladser ja er noget der bliver altså hele tiden bliver 
et større og større problem. Og er det egentlig et aktuelt problem nu til dags? Så Jeg vil sige, 
hvis. 
Du hvis du kigger. Hvis du kigger på de statistikker inden for byggeriet, der Der er 
tilgængelige jamen så er det jo 1 1 1 kæmpe problem at at Der er mange der kommer. Galt 
afsted på byggepladser og og II ganske få tilfælde er. Det jo fortalt. At folk dør ligefrem, ikke 
og og Det er. Jo på ingen måde acceptabelt. 
OK og hvilke slags ulykker er det i Sådan i hører allermest om, som finder sted på specifikt

==PAGE:200==
Page 199 of 246 
 
Appendix 9 – 3F interview transcription 
- 
Kan du fortælle lidt om hvem i er og hvad i gør? 
I 3F Byggegruppen har vi ansat en stribe konsulenter til at varetage vores 
medlemmers interesser. Idet der er mange forskellige interesser, er der også 
forskellige konsulenter, og Flemming Hansen og jeg selv, Anton Helland 
Christiansen, er arbejdsmiljøkonsulenter og fokuserer udelukkende på at løfte 
medlemmers ønsker og behov på området. 
- 
Synes i at ulykker på byggepladser sker ofte og er et aktuelt problem? 
 
Ulykker på byggepladser er alt for ofte forekommende, og har omfattende 
konsekvenser. Både for vores medlemmers helbred, sundhed og økonomi, 
men ofte for virksomhederne der mister mange penge på at have deres ansatte 
til at gå syge, og desuden mister penge i form af tabt produktion. 
 
Byggebranchens ulykkesfrekvens er den dobbelte af det øvrige arbejdsmarked 
og ulykkerne har en større alvorlighedsgrad end gennemsnittet. Dette er, 
modsat industrien, en tendens vi ikke har formået et ændre på de sidste 30 år. 
Og når jeg siger vi mener jeg branchen som helhed. 
 
- 
Hvilke slags ulykker oplever i/har i hørt om finder oftest sted på byggepladser? 
 
Vi er i tæt kontakt med Arbejdstilsynet om vores område, og får de seneste tal 
og tendenser. De hyppigst forekommende ulykker handler om faldulykker, 
både fald fra et niveau til et andet, men også bare fald i samme niveau. Når der 
er mange fald i byggebranchen, handler det i høj grad om at al færdsel foregår 
på en konstant forandrende arbejdsplads. Det betyder desværre at der roder 
meget på en byggeplads, og der er mange niveauforskelle i løbet af 
byggeprocessen. En håndværker går typisk også mange skridt på en 
arbejdsdag, hvilket øger risikoperioden. Ligesådan bærer håndværkere tit på 
noget, hvilket også nedsætter udsynet til gangarealerne.  
- 
Synes i at ulykker hvor køretøjer og kraner (dumpere, gravemaskiner osv) er 
involveret, er noget som sker ofte og er et aktuelt problem? 
Der bliver brugt rigtig mange store maskiner i byggeriet, og derfor er der 
selvfølgelig risici for ulykker der involverer køretøjer, kraner og maskiner. 
Heldigvis er langt de fleste førere af maskinerne både erfarne og dygtige. Der 
er desuden i flere tilfælde krav om certifikater for at betjene større maskiner. 
Dette hæver naturligvis også sikkerheden. Men desværre er uheldet nogle 
gange ude, og vi ser stadig mange ulykker der involverer store maskiner. 
- 
Gør i noget fra jeres side, for at forhindre ulykke og forebygge sikkerheden på 
byggepladser? Hvis ja – Hvad gør i? 
 
I 3F Byggegruppen holder vi mange kurser for vores medlemmer, ligesom vi 
rådgiver vores medlemmer ude i afdelingerne rundt i landet. Vi kører desuden 
et treårigt projekt hvor vi har fem ansatte til udelukkende at køre rundt på 
==PAGE:201==
Page 200 of 246 
 
byggepladser og hjælpe vores medlemmer med deres sikkerhed. Vi kalder 
denne kampagne: ”Er du sikker? – Stil krav til dit arbejdsmiljø” Dette er vores 
direkte forebyggende indsats. 
 
Vi sidder desuden med i flere forskellige organer hvis opgave det er at 
forebygge og forhindre ulykker. Her kan blandt andet nævnes Byggeriets 
Arbejdsmiljøbus (BAMBUS), som er et sekretariat med 10 udkørende 
konsulenter, der er partsneutralt og dialogorienteret. Disse konsulenter kan 
tilkaldes af både arbejdsgiverne og af vores medlemmer, og skal rådgive 
løsningsorienteret.  
 
Ligesådan vil jeg nævne Branchefælleskabet for Arbejdsmiljø – Bygge&Anlæg 
(BFA-BA), der også er partsneutralt, og som i samarbejde mellem parterne og 
arbejdstilsynet, udarbejder, udvikler og distribuerer omfattende 
vejledningsmateriale, der er branchenært, gennembearbejdet og godkendt af 
alle byggeriets parter som værende ’best practice’. Det er i øvrigt tit 
BFAmaterialer der refereres til hos arbejdstilsynet, ligesom der tit føres tilsyn 
baseret på de enkelte branchevejledninger. 
 
Endeligt bør jeg også nævne Under Hjelmene, som er parternes fælles 
arbejdsmiljøavis, der udkommer to gange årligt. Avisen forsøger at belyse 
konkrete problemstillinger i byggebranchen, fremhæve gode løsninger, og 
sætte fokus på den nyeste udvikling af regler, lovgivning osv. Avisen 
udkommer i et oplæg på ca. 40.000 eksemplarer og er alment kendt i 
branchen.  
 
De tre ovenstående er blandt vores mere indirekte forebyggende indsatser. 
- 
Synes i at i kan gøre mere for at fremme sikkerheden på byggepladser? Hvis ja – 
Hvad? 
 
Arbejdsmiljøet er jo en diffus størrelse. Dels fordi der er mange regler der ikke 
er helt sort-hvide. Dels fordi reglerne fortolkes og overholdes meget 
individuelt. Vi gør selvfølgelig hvad vi kan for at forbedre sikkerhed på et 
generelt plan, ved at skubbe på for strammere arbejdsmiljølovgivning, politisk 
fokus og gennem drøftelser med virksomhederne lokalt. Men jeg synes det er 
meget vigtigt at pointere at fagbevægelsen har meget lidt direkte indflydelse 
på vores enkelte medlems egen sikkerhed. Det er en opgave de selv må 
varetage, ligesom de skal have hjælp af deres arbejdsmiljørepræsentant og 
deres arbejdsgiver, der har ansvaret i sidste ende. 
 
Så kan man måske grave sig dybere ned i hvad arbejdsmiljøorganisationerne 
ude på byggepladserne gør og om de overholder deres opgaver, men det er nok 
en diskussion til en anden dag. 
- 
Hvad er jeres holdning til implementering af avanceret teknologi (lokationsbaseret 
sensorer på arbejdere og maskineri eller kameraer på maskineri)  til optimering af 
sikkerheden på byggepladsen? 
Det er superfedt at I har taget dette med i jeres spørgsmål, og det er helt 
bestemt et felt der kommer til at blive bredt meget mere ud over de næste år. 
==PAGE:202==
Page 201 of 246 
 
Vi er selv kun lige begyndt at få øjnene op for sensorers potentiale indenfor 
arbejdsmiljøet, men der er ingen tvivl om at det er et stærkt værktøj.  
Der er dog en ærgerlig ulempe ved GPS’er og kameraer i byggeriet. Det 
kommer nemlig til tider til at glide over i et overvågningsværktøj, der kan få 
konsekvenser for de ansattes lønforhold og til tider lede til fyringer. Denne 
slags overvågning er jo strengt reguleret af blandt andet 
datasikkerhedsforordningen, og stiller vidtrækkende krav til arbejdsgivernes 
behandling af indsamlede data. Vi har for nyligt lavet en spørgeundersøgelse i 
3F, hvor vi har spurgt vores medlemmer om overvågning. 71 % af 
respondenterne fra Byggegruppen skriver at de har overvågning på deres 
kørsel i firmabilerne. Vi har desværre også allerede haft faglige sager med den 
slags.  
Drømmen ift. implementering af sensorer i byggeriet, er jo f.eks. at maskinen 
stopper af sig selv hvis den kan se at den er ved at køre en kollega ned, køre en 
ledning over eller vælte noget. Her kan teknologien jo være en kæmpe hjælp, 
og være med til at forhindre potentielt tragiske ulykker. 
Jeg drømmer også om elektroniske støvmålere der kan advare medarbejderne 
om at støvniveauet i bygningen har nået et sundhedsskadeligt niveau.  
Hvad er jeres kunders holdning til det? 
Det er min personlige vurdering at vores medlemmer stadig bekymrer sig så 
meget om alle de ting på byggepladsen der kan slå dem ihjel eller invalidere 
dem, at de ’blødere’ problemer som f.eks. overvågning, ikke fylder så meget i 
Byggegruppen. Men som medarbejdergruppe, tænker jeg at de er hurtige til at 
implementere ny teknologi og nye værktøjer. Hvis der kommer noget nyt på 
markedet der kan hjælpe dem i deres arbejde, eller gøre dem mere sikre, tager 
de som regel godt imod det. 
- 
Synes i at implementeringen af disse teknologier vil kunne fremme sikkerheden på 
byggepladser? 
Ja bestemt. Men igen skal vi være gode til at bruge teknologien på den rigtige 
måde. Jeg synes også jeg har svaret på det ovenfor. 
- 
Synes i at implementeringen af disse teknologier vil være det værd, på trods af de 
omkostninger der kan forekomme ved installering og vedligeholdelse af disse 
teknologier? 
Vores medlemmer har jo ikke nogen udgifter ifm. denne implementering. Men 
generelt kan jeg måske sige om branchen, at der ikke er nogen stor 
overskudsgrad, og derfor bruges der sjældent penge på teknologier der ikke 
umiddelbart kan tjene sig ind. Det skal være brugbart og effektivt før de 
kommer til at vinde indpas i branchen. 
- 
Hvilke komplikationer vil der kunne forekomme ved implementering af 
lokationsbaseret sensorer og kameraer, både fra et moralsk og et juridisk synspunkt. 
Tillader lovgivningen det? 
==PAGE:203==
Page 202 of 246 
 
Det er jeg nok ikke den rigtige at spørge om, men som nævnt ovenfor er der 
helt sikkert nogle knaster ift. dataindsamling af medarbejdere. 
- 
Kan disse komplikationer overkommes? Hvis ja – Hvordan? 
Som ovenfor ☺
